I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: 72.331*epsilon² + 7.747*epsilon*sin(T - 287.774)**

Note that sin(T - 287.774) can be rewritten using trig identities. Since 287.774 is a constant, sin(T - 287.774) = sin(T)cos(287.774) - cos(T)sin(287.774). So the GT can be written as:

**GT = 72.331*epsilon² + epsilon*(A*sin(T) + B*cos(T))**

where A = 7.747*cos(287.774) and B = -7.747*sin(287.774). This means any candidate that can express `c*epsilon² + epsilon*(a*sin(T) + b*cos(T))` is equivalent.

Equivalently, `epsilon*(c*epsilon + a*sin(T) + b*cos(T))` or `epsilon*(c*epsilon + d*sin(T + phase))`.

Let me check each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** 72.331*epsilon*(T*c0*cos(T+c1) + c2*cos(T+c1) + c3*epsilon*cos(T+c1) + c4*cos(T) + epsilon)
Contains T*cos(T+c1) term which can't be zeroed without zeroing c0 alone. Setting c0=0, we get 72.331*epsilon*(c2*cos(T+c1) + c3*epsilon*cos(T+c1) + c4*cos(T) + epsilon). The c3*epsilon*cos(T+c1) term gives epsilon²*cos(T+c1) which isn't in GT. Set c3=0: 72.331*epsilon*(c2*cos(T+c1) + c4*cos(T) + epsilon) = 72.331*epsilon² + 72.331*epsilon*(c2*cos(T+c1) + c4*cos(T)). cos(T+c1) = cos(T)cos(c1) - sin(T)sin(c1). So this gives epsilon*(a*sin(T) + b*cos(T)) + 72.331*epsilon². This matches!
**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 2:** epsilon*(T*c0*cos(T+c1) + c2*cos(T+c1) + c3*cos(T+c2) + c4*epsilon*cos(T+c1) + 72.331*epsilon)
Set c0=0, c4=0: epsilon*(c2*cos(T+c1) + c3*cos(T+c2) + 72.331*epsilon). This gives 72.331*epsilon² + epsilon*(c2*cos(T+c1) + c3*cos(T+c2)). Two cosines with different phases can produce a*sin(T)+b*cos(T). Yes, this matches!
**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 3:** epsilon*(T*c0*cos(T+1) + c0*sin(T+c1) + c2*cos(T+1) + c3*epsilon*cos(T+1) + 72.331*epsilon)
The T*c0*cos(T+1) term: setting c0=0 kills both T*cos and sin terms. Then: epsilon*(c2*cos(T+1) + c3*epsilon*cos(T+1) + 72.331*epsilon). The c3*epsilon*cos(T+1) gives epsilon²*cos which isn't in GT. Set c3=0: epsilon*(c2*cos(T+1) + 72.331*epsilon) = 72.331*epsilon² + c2*epsilon*cos(T+1). But cos(T+1) alone can't produce both sin(T) and cos(T) independently. We only get one degree of freedom for the trig part. We need epsilon*(a*sin(T)+b*cos(T)) but cos(T+1) = cos(T)cos(1)-sin(T)sin(1), giving a fixed ratio. The GT has specific A,B values - we'd need c2 such that c2*cos(1) = B and -c2*sin(1) = A. This constrains A/B = -tan(1), which may not match GT. Actually, sin(T+c2) with free c2 would work, but here c0 is shared. If c0≠0, we get T*c0*cos(T+1) which is unwanted. So this likely doesn't match.
**Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 4:** Has many terms. Setting c0=0, c5=0: c2*cos(T+c3) + c4*epsilon*cos(T+c3) + 72.331*epsilon². The c2*cos and c4*epsilon*cos terms - c2 can be set to 0. Then c4*epsilon*cos(T+c3) + 72.331*epsilon². cos(T+c3) with free c3 gives one trig function with adjustable phase = sin(T+phase). This matches!
**Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]**
